- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `gateway.http.endpoints.responses.maxUrlParts`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `gateway.mode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Gateway operation mode: "local" runs channels and agent runtime on this host, while "remote" connects through remote transport. Keep "local" unless you intentionally run a split remote gateway topology.

### `gateway.nodes`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `gateway.nodes.allowCommands`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Extra node.invoke commands to allow beyond the gateway defaults (array of command strings). Enabling dangerous commands here is a security-sensitive override and is flagged by `openclaw security audit`.

### `gateway.nodes.allowCommands[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `gateway.nodes.browser`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `gateway.nodes.browser.mode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Node browser routing ("auto" = pick single connected browser node, "manual" = require node param, "off" = disable).

### `gateway.nodes.browser.node`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Pin browser routing to a specific node id or name (optional).

### `gateway.nodes.denyCommands`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Commands to block even if present in node claims or default allowlist.

### `gateway.nodes.denyCommands[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `gateway.port`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: TCP port used by the gateway listener for API, control UI, and channel-facing ingress paths. Use a dedicated port and avoid collisions with reverse proxies or local developer services.

### `gateway.reload`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Live config-reload policy for how edits are applied and when full restarts are triggered. Keep hybrid behavior for safest operational updates unless debugging reload internals.

### `gateway.reload.debounceMs`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Debounce window (ms) before applying config changes.

### `gateway.reload.mode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Controls how config edits are applied: "off" ignores live edits, "restart" always restarts, "hot" applies in-process, and "hybrid" tries hot then restarts if required. Keep "hybrid" for safest routine updates.

### `gateway.remote`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Remote gateway connection settings for direct or SSH transport when this instance proxies to another runtime host. Use remote mode only when split-host operation is intentionally configured.

### `gateway.remote.password`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Password credential used for remote gateway authentication when password mode is enabled. Keep this secret managed externally and avoid plaintext values in committed config.

### `gateway.remote.sshIdentity`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional SSH identity file path (passed to ssh -i).

### `gateway.remote.sshTarget`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Remote gateway over SSH (tunnels the gateway port to localhost). Format: user@host or user@host:port.

### `gateway.remote.tlsFingerprint`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Expected sha256 TLS fingerprint for the remote gateway (pin to avoid MITM).

### `gateway.remote.token`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Bearer token used to authenticate this client to a remote gateway in token-auth deployments. Store via secret/env substitution and rotate alongside remote gateway auth changes.

### `gateway.remote.transport`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Remote connection transport: "direct" uses configured URL connectivity, while "ssh" tunnels through SSH. Use SSH when you need encrypted tunnel semantics without exposing remote ports.

### `gateway.remote.url`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Remote Gateway WebSocket URL (ws:// or wss://).

### `gateway.tailscale`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Tailscale integration settings for Serve/Funnel exposure and lifecycle handling on gateway start/exit. Keep off unless your deployment intentionally relies on Tailscale ingress.

### `gateway.tailscale.mode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Tailscale publish mode: "off", "serve", or "funnel" for private or public exposure paths. Use "serve" for tailnet-only access and "funnel" only when public internet reachability is required.

### `gateway.tailscale.resetOnExit`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Resets Tailscale Serve/Funnel state on gateway exit to avoid stale published routes after shutdown. Keep enabled unless another controller manages publish lifecycle outside the gateway.

### `gateway.tls`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: TLS certificate and key settings for terminating HTTPS directly in the gateway process. Use explicit certificates in production and avoid plaintext exposure on untrusted networks.

### `gateway.tls.autoGenerate`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Auto-generates a local TLS certificate/key pair when explicit files are not configured. Use only for local/dev setups and replace with real certificates for production traffic.

### `gateway.tls.caPath`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional CA bundle path for client verification or custom trust-chain requirements at the gateway edge. Use this when private PKI or custom certificate chains are part of deployment.

### `gateway.tls.certPath`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Filesystem path to the TLS certificate file used by the gateway when TLS is enabled. Use managed certificate paths and keep renewal automation aligned with this location.

### `gateway.tls.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Enables TLS termination at the gateway listener so clients connect over HTTPS/WSS directly. Keep enabled for direct internet exposure or any untrusted network boundary.

### `gateway.tls.keyPath`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Filesystem path to the TLS private key file used by the gateway when TLS is enabled. Keep this key file permission-restricted and rotate per your security policy.

### `gateway.tools`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Gateway-level tool exposure allow/deny policy that can restrict runtime tool availability independent of agent/tool profiles. Use this for coarse emergency controls and production hardening.

### `gateway.tools.allow`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Explicit gateway-level tool allowlist when you want a narrow set of tools available at runtime. Use this for locked-down environments where tool scope must be tightly controlled.

### `gateway.tools.allow[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `gateway.tools.deny`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Explicit gateway-level tool denylist to block risky tools even if lower-level policies allow them. Use deny rules for emergency response and defense-in-depth hardening.

### `gateway.tools.deny[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `gateway.trustedProxies`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: CIDR/IP allowlist of upstream proxies permitted to provide forwarded client identity headers. Keep this list narrow so untrusted hops cannot impersonate users.

### `gateway.trustedProxies[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

## Hooks

Inbound webhook automation surface for mapping external events into wake or agent actions in OpenClaw. Keep this locked down with explicit token/session/agent controls before exposing it beyond trusted networks.

### `hooks`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Inbound webhook automation surface for mapping external events into wake or agent actions in OpenClaw. Keep this locked down with explicit token/session/agent controls before exposing it beyond trusted networks.

### `hooks.allowedAgentIds`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Allowlist of agent IDs that hook mappings are allowed to target when selecting execution agents. Use this to constrain automation events to dedicated service agents.

### `hooks.allowedAgentIds[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.allowedSessionKeyPrefixes`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Allowlist of accepted session-key prefixes for inbound hook requests when caller-provided keys are enabled. Use narrow prefixes to prevent arbitrary session-key injection.

### `hooks.allowedSessionKeyPrefixes[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.allowRequestSessionKey`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Allows callers to supply a session key in hook requests when true, enabling caller-controlled routing. Keep false unless trusted integrators explicitly need custom session threading.

### `hooks.defaultSessionKey`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Fallback session key used for hook deliveries when a request does not provide one through allowed channels. Use a stable but scoped key to avoid mixing unrelated automation conversations.

### `hooks.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Enables the hooks endpoint and mapping execution pipeline for inbound webhook requests. Keep disabled unless you are actively routing external events into the gateway.

### `hooks.gmail`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Gmail push integration settings used for Pub/Sub notifications and optional local callback serving. Keep this scoped to dedicated Gmail automation accounts where possible.

### `hooks.gmail.account`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Google account identifier used for Gmail watch/subscription operations in this hook integration. Use a dedicated automation mailbox account to isolate operational permissions.

### `hooks.gmail.allowUnsafeExternalContent`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Allows less-sanitized external Gmail content to pass into processing when enabled. Keep disabled for safer defaults, and enable only for trusted mail streams with controlled transforms.

### `hooks.gmail.hookUrl`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Public callback URL Gmail or intermediaries invoke to deliver notifications into this hook pipeline. Keep this URL protected with token validation and restricted network exposure.

### `hooks.gmail.includeBody`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: When true, fetch and include email body content for downstream mapping/agent processing. Keep false unless body text is required, because this increases payload size and sensitivity.

### `hooks.gmail.label`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional Gmail label filter limiting which labeled messages trigger hook events. Keep filters narrow to avoid flooding automations with unrelated inbox traffic.

### `hooks.gmail.maxBytes`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Maximum Gmail payload bytes processed per event when includeBody is enabled. Keep conservative limits to reduce oversized message processing cost and risk.

### `hooks.gmail.model`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional model override for Gmail-triggered runs when mailbox automations should use dedicated model behavior. Keep unset to inherit agent defaults unless mailbox tasks need specialization.

### `hooks.gmail.pushToken`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Shared secret token required on Gmail push hook callbacks before processing notifications. Use env substitution and rotate if callback endpoints are exposed externally.

### `hooks.gmail.renewEveryMinutes`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Renewal cadence in minutes for Gmail watch subscriptions to prevent expiration. Set below provider expiration windows and monitor renew failures in logs.

### `hooks.gmail.serve`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Local callback server settings block for directly receiving Gmail notifications without a separate ingress layer. Enable only when this process should terminate webhook traffic itself.

### `hooks.gmail.serve.bind`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Bind address for the local Gmail callback HTTP server used when serving hooks directly. Keep loopback-only unless external ingress is intentionally required.

### `hooks.gmail.serve.path`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: HTTP path on the local Gmail callback server where push notifications are accepted. Keep this consistent with subscription configuration to avoid dropped events.

### `hooks.gmail.serve.port`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Port for the local Gmail callback HTTP server when serve mode is enabled. Use a dedicated port to avoid collisions with gateway/control interfaces.

### `hooks.gmail.subscription`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Pub/Sub subscription consumed by the gateway to receive Gmail change notifications from the configured topic. Keep subscription ownership clear so multiple consumers do not race unexpectedly.

### `hooks.gmail.tailscale`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Tailscale exposure configuration block for publishing Gmail callbacks through Serve/Funnel routes. Use private tailnet modes before enabling any public ingress path.

### `hooks.gmail.tailscale.mode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Tailscale exposure mode for Gmail callbacks: "off", "serve", or "funnel". Use "serve" for private tailnet delivery and "funnel" only when public internet ingress is required.

### `hooks.gmail.tailscale.path`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Path published by Tailscale Serve/Funnel for Gmail callback forwarding when enabled. Keep it aligned with Gmail webhook config so requests reach the expected handler.

### `hooks.gmail.tailscale.target`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Local service target forwarded by Tailscale Serve/Funnel (for example [http://127.0.0.1:8787](http://127.0.0.1:8787)). Use explicit loopback targets to avoid ambiguous routing.

### `hooks.gmail.thinking`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Thinking effort override for Gmail-driven agent runs: "off", "minimal", "low", "medium", or "high". Keep modest defaults for routine inbox automations to control cost and latency.

### `hooks.gmail.topic`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Google Pub/Sub topic name used by Gmail watch to publish change notifications for this account. Ensure the topic IAM grants Gmail publish access before enabling watches.

### `hooks.internal`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Internal hook runtime settings for bundled/custom event handlers loaded from module paths. Use this for trusted in-process automations and keep handler loading tightly scoped.

### `hooks.internal.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Enables processing for internal hook handlers and configured entries in the internal hook runtime. Keep disabled unless internal hook handlers are intentionally configured.

### `hooks.internal.entries`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Configured internal hook entry records used to register concrete runtime handlers and metadata. Keep entries explicit and versioned so production behavior is auditable.

### `hooks.internal.entries.*`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.internal.entries.*.*`

- Type: `any`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.internal.entries.*.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.internal.entries.*.env`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.internal.entries.*.env.*`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.internal.handlers`

- Type: `array<object>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: List of internal event handlers mapping event names to modules and optional exports. Keep handler definitions explicit so event-to-code routing is auditable.

### `hooks.internal.handlers[]`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.internal.handlers[].event`

- Type: `string`
- Required: yes
- Default: _none_
- Description: Internal event name that triggers this handler module when emitted by the runtime. Use stable event naming conventions to avoid accidental overlap across handlers.

### `hooks.internal.handlers[].export`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional named export for the internal hook handler function when module default export is not used. Set this when one module ships multiple handler entrypoints.

### `hooks.internal.handlers[].module`

- Type: `string`
- Required: yes
- Default: _none_
- Description: Safe relative module path for the internal hook handler implementation loaded at runtime. Keep module files in reviewed directories and avoid dynamic path composition.

### `hooks.internal.installs`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Install metadata for internal hook modules, including source and resolved artifacts for repeatable deployments. Use this as operational provenance and avoid manual drift edits.

### `hooks.internal.installs.*`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.internal.installs.*.hooks`

- Required: no
- Default: _none_

### `hooks.internal.load`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Internal hook loader settings controlling where handler modules are discovered at startup. Use constrained load roots to reduce accidental module conflicts or shadowing.

### `hooks.internal.load.extraDirs`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Additional directories searched for internal hook modules beyond default load paths. Keep this minimal and controlled to reduce accidental module shadowing.

### `hooks.internal.load.extraDirs[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.mappings`

- Type: `array<object>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Ordered mapping rules that match inbound hook requests and choose wake or agent actions with optional delivery routing. Use specific mappings first to avoid broad pattern rules capturing everything.

### `hooks.mappings[]`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.mappings[].action`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Mapping action type: "wake" triggers agent wake flow, while "agent" sends directly to agent handling. Use "agent" for immediate execution and "wake" when heartbeat-driven processing is preferred.

### `hooks.mappings[].agentId`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Target agent ID for mapping execution when action routing should not use defaults. Use dedicated automation agents to isolate webhook behavior from interactive operator sessions.

### `hooks.mappings[].allowUnsafeExternalContent`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: When true, mapping content may include less-sanitized external payload data in generated messages. Keep false by default and enable only for trusted sources with reviewed transform logic.

### `hooks.mappings[].channel`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Delivery channel override for mapping outputs (for example "last", "telegram", "discord", "slack", "signal", "imessage", or "msteams"). Keep channel overrides explicit to avoid accidental cross-channel sends.

### `hooks.mappings[].deliver`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Controls whether mapping execution results are delivered back to a channel destination versus being processed silently. Disable delivery for background automations that should not post user-facing output.

### `hooks.mappings[].id`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional stable identifier for a hook mapping entry used for auditing, troubleshooting, and targeted updates. Use unique IDs so logs and config diffs can reference mappings unambiguously.

### `hooks.mappings[].match`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Grouping object for mapping match predicates such as path and source before action routing is applied. Keep match criteria specific so unrelated webhook traffic does not trigger automations.

### `hooks.mappings[].match.path`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Path match condition for a hook mapping, usually compared against the inbound request path. Use this to split automation behavior by webhook endpoint path families.

### `hooks.mappings[].match.source`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Source match condition for a hook mapping, typically set by trusted upstream metadata or adapter logic. Use stable source identifiers so routing remains deterministic across retries.

### `hooks.mappings[].messageTemplate`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Template for synthesizing structured mapping input into the final message content sent to the target action path. Keep templates deterministic so downstream parsing and behavior remain stable.

### `hooks.mappings[].model`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional model override for mapping-triggered runs when automation should use a different model than agent defaults. Use this sparingly so behavior remains predictable across mapping executions.

### `hooks.mappings[].name`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Human-readable mapping display name used in diagnostics and operator-facing config UIs. Keep names concise and descriptive so routing intent is obvious during incident review.

### `hooks.mappings[].sessionKey`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Explicit session key override for mapping-delivered messages to control thread continuity. Use stable scoped keys so repeated events correlate without leaking into unrelated conversations.

### `hooks.mappings[].textTemplate`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Text-only fallback template used when rich payload rendering is not desired or not supported. Use this to provide a concise, consistent summary string for chat delivery surfaces.

### `hooks.mappings[].thinking`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional thinking-effort override for mapping-triggered runs to tune latency versus reasoning depth. Keep low or minimal for high-volume hooks unless deeper reasoning is clearly required.

### `hooks.mappings[].timeoutSeconds`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Maximum runtime allowed for mapping action execution before timeout handling applies. Use tighter limits for high-volume webhook sources to prevent queue pileups.

### `hooks.mappings[].to`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Destination identifier inside the selected channel when mapping replies should route to a fixed target. Verify provider-specific destination formats before enabling production mappings.

### `hooks.mappings[].transform`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Transform configuration block defining module/export preprocessing before mapping action handling. Use transforms only from reviewed code paths and keep behavior deterministic for repeatable automation.

### `hooks.mappings[].transform.export`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Named export to invoke from the transform module; defaults to module default export when omitted. Set this when one file hosts multiple transform handlers.

### `hooks.mappings[].transform.module`

- Type: `string`
- Required: yes
- Default: _none_
- Description: Relative transform module path loaded from hooks.transformsDir to rewrite incoming payloads before delivery. Keep modules local, reviewed, and free of path traversal patterns.

### `hooks.mappings[].wakeMode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Wake scheduling mode: "now" wakes immediately, while "next-heartbeat" defers until the next heartbeat cycle. Use deferred mode for lower-priority automations that can tolerate slight delay.

### `hooks.maxBodyBytes`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Maximum accepted webhook payload size in bytes before the request is rejected. Keep this bounded to reduce abuse risk and protect memory usage under bursty integrations.

### `hooks.path`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: HTTP path used by the hooks endpoint (for example `/hooks`) on the gateway control server. Use a non-guessable path and combine it with token validation for defense in depth.

### `hooks.presets`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Named hook preset bundles applied at load time to seed standard mappings and behavior defaults. Keep preset usage explicit so operators can audit which automations are active.

### `hooks.presets[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `hooks.token`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Shared bearer token checked by hooks ingress for request authentication before mappings run. Use environment substitution and rotate regularly when webhook endpoints are internet-accessible.

### `hooks.transformsDir`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Base directory for hook transform modules referenced by mapping transform.module paths. Use a controlled repo directory so dynamic imports remain reviewable and predictable.

## Logging

Logging behavior controls for severity, output destinations, formatting, and sensitive-data redaction. Keep levels and redaction strict enough for production while preserving useful diagnostics.

### `logging`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Logging behavior controls for severity, output destinations, formatting, and sensitive-data redaction. Keep levels and redaction strict enough for production while preserving useful diagnostics.

### `logging.consoleLevel`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Console-specific log threshold: "silent", "fatal", "error", "warn", "info", "debug", or "trace" for terminal output control. Use this to keep local console quieter while retaining richer file logging if needed.

### `logging.consoleStyle`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Console output format style: "pretty", "compact", or "json" based on operator and ingestion needs. Use json for machine parsing pipelines and pretty/compact for human-first terminal workflows.

### `logging.file`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional file path for persisted log output in addition to or instead of console logging. Use a managed writable path and align retention/rotation with your operational policy.

### `logging.level`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Primary log level threshold for runtime logger output: "silent", "fatal", "error", "warn", "info", "debug", or "trace". Keep "info" or "warn" for production, and use debug/trace only during investigation.

### `logging.maxFileBytes`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `logging.redactPatterns`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Additional custom redact regex patterns applied to log output before emission/storage. Use this to mask org-specific tokens and identifiers not covered by built-in redaction rules.

### `logging.redactPatterns[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `logging.redactSensitive`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sensitive redaction mode: "off" disables built-in masking, while "tools" redacts sensitive tool/config payload fields. Keep "tools" in shared logs unless you have isolated secure log sinks.

## Media

Top-level media behavior shared across providers and tools that handle inbound files. Keep defaults unless you need stable filenames for external processing pipelines.

### `media`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Top-level media behavior shared across providers and tools that handle inbound files. Keep defaults unless you need stable filenames for external processing pipelines.

### `media.preserveFilenames`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: When enabled, uploaded media keeps its original filename instead of a generated temp-safe name. Turn this on when downstream automations depend on stable names, and leave off to reduce accidental filename leakage.

## Memory

Memory backend configuration (global).

### `memory`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Memory backend configuration (global).

### `memory.backend`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Selects the global memory engine: "builtin" uses OpenClaw memory internals, while "qmd" uses the QMD sidecar pipeline. Keep "builtin" unless you intentionally operate QMD.

### `memory.citations`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Controls citation visibility in replies: "auto" shows citations when useful, "on" always shows them, and "off" hides them. Keep "auto" for a balanced signal-to-noise default.

### `memory.qmd`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `memory.qmd.command`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sets the executable path for the `qmd` binary used by the QMD backend (default: resolved from PATH). Use an explicit absolute path when multiple qmd installs exist or PATH differs across environments.

### `memory.qmd.includeDefaultMemory`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Automatically indexes default memory files (MEMORY.md and memory/\*\*/\*.md) into QMD collections. Keep enabled unless you want indexing controlled only through explicit custom paths.

### `memory.qmd.limits`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `memory.qmd.limits.maxInjectedChars`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Caps how much QMD text can be injected into one turn across all hits. Use lower values to control prompt bloat and latency; raise only when context is consistently truncated.

### `memory.qmd.limits.maxResults`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Limits how many QMD hits are returned into the agent loop for each recall request (default: 6). Increase for broader recall context, or lower to keep prompts tighter and faster.

### `memory.qmd.limits.maxSnippetChars`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Caps per-result snippet length extracted from QMD hits in characters (default: 700). Lower this when prompts bloat quickly, and raise only if answers consistently miss key details.

### `memory.qmd.limits.timeoutMs`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sets per-query QMD search timeout in milliseconds (default: 4000). Increase for larger indexes or slower environments, and lower to keep request latency bounded.

### `memory.qmd.mcporter`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Routes QMD work through mcporter (MCP runtime) instead of spawning `qmd` for each call. Use this when cold starts are expensive on large models; keep direct process mode for simpler local setups.

### `memory.qmd.mcporter.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Routes QMD through an mcporter daemon instead of spawning qmd per request, reducing cold-start overhead for larger models. Keep disabled unless mcporter is installed and configured.

### `memory.qmd.mcporter.serverName`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Names the mcporter server target used for QMD calls (default: qmd). Change only when your mcporter setup uses a custom server name for qmd mcp keep-alive.

### `memory.qmd.mcporter.startDaemon`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Automatically starts the mcporter daemon when mcporter-backed QMD mode is enabled (default: true). Keep enabled unless process lifecycle is managed externally by your service supervisor.

### `memory.qmd.paths`

- Type: `array<object>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Adds custom directories or files to include in QMD indexing, each with an optional name and glob pattern. Use this for project-specific knowledge locations that are outside default memory paths.

### `memory.qmd.paths[]`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `memory.qmd.paths[].name`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `memory.qmd.paths[].path`

- Type: `string`
- Required: yes
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `memory.qmd.paths[].pattern`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `memory.qmd.scope`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Defines which sessions/channels are eligible for QMD recall using session.sendPolicy-style rules. Keep default direct-only scope unless you intentionally want cross-chat memory sharing.

### `memory.qmd.searchMode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Selects the QMD retrieval path: "query" uses standard query flow, "search" uses search-oriented retrieval, and "vsearch" emphasizes vector retrieval. Keep default unless tuning relevance quality.

### `memory.qmd.sessions`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `memory.qmd.sessions.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Indexes session transcripts into QMD so recall can include prior conversation content (experimental, default: false). Enable only when transcript memory is required and you accept larger index churn.

### `memory.qmd.sessions.exportDir`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Overrides where sanitized session exports are written before QMD indexing. Use this when default state storage is constrained or when exports must land on a managed volume.

### `memory.qmd.sessions.retentionDays`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Defines how long exported session files are kept before automatic pruning, in days (default: unlimited). Set a finite value for storage hygiene or compliance retention policies.

### `memory.qmd.update`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `memory.qmd.update.commandTimeoutMs`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sets timeout for QMD maintenance commands such as collection list/add in milliseconds (default: 30000). Increase when running on slower disks or remote filesystems that delay command completion.

### `memory.qmd.update.debounceMs`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sets the minimum delay between consecutive QMD refresh attempts in milliseconds (default: 15000). Increase this if frequent file changes cause update thrash or unnecessary background load.

### `memory.qmd.update.embedInterval`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sets how often QMD recomputes embeddings (duration string, default: 60m; set 0 to disable periodic embeds). Lower intervals improve freshness but increase embedding workload and cost.

### `memory.qmd.update.embedTimeoutMs`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sets maximum runtime for each `qmd embed` cycle in milliseconds (default: 120000). Increase for heavier embedding workloads or slower hardware, and lower to fail fast under tight SLAs.

### `memory.qmd.update.interval`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sets how often QMD refreshes indexes from source content (duration string, default: 5m). Shorter intervals improve freshness but increase background CPU and I/O.

### `memory.qmd.update.onBoot`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Runs an initial QMD update once during gateway startup (default: true). Keep enabled so recall starts from a fresh baseline; disable only when startup speed is more important than immediate freshness.

### `memory.qmd.update.updateTimeoutMs`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sets maximum runtime for each `qmd update` cycle in milliseconds (default: 120000). Raise this for larger collections; lower it when you want quicker failure detection in automation.

### `memory.qmd.update.waitForBootSync`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Blocks startup completion until the initial boot-time QMD sync finishes (default: false). Enable when you need fully up-to-date recall before serving traffic, and keep off for faster boot.

## Messages

Message formatting, acknowledgment, queueing, debounce, and status reaction behavior for inbound/outbound chat flows. Use this section when channel responsiveness or message UX needs adjustment.

### `messages`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Message formatting, acknowledgment, queueing, debounce, and status reaction behavior for inbound/outbound chat flows. Use this section when channel responsiveness or message UX needs adjustment.

### `messages.ackReaction`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Emoji reaction used to acknowledge inbound messages (empty disables).

### `messages.ackReactionScope`

- Type: `"group-mentions" | "group-all" | "direct" | "all"`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: When to send ack reactions ("group-mentions", "group-all", "direct", "all").

### `messages.groupChat`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Group-message handling controls including mention triggers and history window sizing. Keep mention patterns narrow so group channels do not trigger on every message.

### `messages.groupChat.historyLimit`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Maximum number of prior group messages loaded as context per turn for group sessions. Use higher values for richer continuity, or lower values for faster and cheaper responses.

### `messages.groupChat.mentionPatterns`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Regex-like patterns used to detect explicit mentions/trigger phrases in group chats. Use precise patterns to reduce false positives in high-volume channels.

### `messages.groupChat.mentionPatterns[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.inbound`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Direct inbound debounce settings used before queue/turn processing starts. Configure this for provider-specific rapid message bursts from the same sender.

### `messages.inbound.byChannel`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Per-channel inbound debounce overrides keyed by provider id in milliseconds. Use this where some providers send message fragments more aggressively than others.

### `messages.inbound.byChannel.*`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.inbound.debounceMs`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Debounce window (ms) for batching rapid inbound messages from the same sender (0 to disable).

### `messages.messagePrefix`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Prefix text prepended to inbound user messages before they are handed to the agent runtime. Use this sparingly for channel context markers and keep it stable across sessions.

### `messages.queue`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Inbound message queue strategy used to buffer bursts before processing turns. Tune this for busy channels where sequential processing or batching behavior matters.

### `messages.queue.byChannel`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Per-channel queue mode overrides keyed by provider id (for example telegram, discord, slack). Use this when one channels traffic pattern needs different queue behavior than global defaults.

### `messages.queue.byChannel.discord`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.byChannel.imessage`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.byChannel.irc`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.byChannel.mattermost`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.byChannel.msteams`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.byChannel.signal`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.byChannel.slack`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.byChannel.telegram`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.byChannel.webchat`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.byChannel.whatsapp`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.cap`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Maximum number of queued inbound items retained before drop policy applies. Keep caps bounded in noisy channels so memory usage remains predictable.

### `messages.queue.debounceMs`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Global queue debounce window in milliseconds before processing buffered inbound messages. Use higher values to coalesce rapid bursts, or lower values for reduced response latency.

### `messages.queue.debounceMsByChannel`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Per-channel debounce overrides for queue behavior keyed by provider id. Use this to tune burst handling independently for chat surfaces with different pacing.

### `messages.queue.debounceMsByChannel.*`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.queue.drop`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Drop strategy when queue cap is exceeded: "old", "new", or "summarize". Use summarize when preserving intent matters, or old/new when deterministic dropping is preferred.

### `messages.queue.mode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Queue behavior mode: "steer", "followup", "collect", "steer-backlog", "steer+backlog", "queue", or "interrupt". Keep conservative modes unless you intentionally need aggressive interruption/backlog semantics.

### `messages.removeAckAfterReply`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Removes the acknowledgment reaction after final reply delivery when enabled. Keep enabled for cleaner UX in channels where persistent ack reactions create clutter.

### `messages.responsePrefix`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Prefix text prepended to outbound assistant replies before sending to channels. Use for lightweight branding/context tags and avoid long prefixes that reduce content density.

### `messages.statusReactions`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Lifecycle status reactions that update the emoji on the trigger message as the agent progresses (queued  thinking  tool  done/error).

### `messages.statusReactions.emojis`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Override default status reaction emojis. Keys: thinking, tool, coding, web, done, error, stallSoft, stallHard. Must be valid Telegram reaction emojis.

### `messages.statusReactions.emojis.coding`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_

- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.statusReactions.emojis.error`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.statusReactions.emojis.stallSoft`

- Type: `string`

- Default: _none_

### `messages.statusReactions.timing.stallSoftMs`

- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `messages.suppressToolErrors`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: When true, suppress  tool-error warnings from being shown to the user. The agent already sees errors in context and can retry. Default: false.

Metadata fields automatically maintained by OpenClaw to record write/version history for this config file. Keep these values system-managed and avoid manual edits unless debugging migration history.

### `meta`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Metadata fields automatically maintained by OpenClaw to record write/version history for this config file. Keep these values system-managed and avoid manual edits unless debugging migration history.

### `meta.lastTouchedAt`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: ISO timestamp of the last config write (auto-set).

### `meta.lastTouchedVersion`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Auto-set when OpenClaw writes the config.

## Models

Model catalog root for provider definitions, merge/replace behavior, and optional Bedrock discovery integration. Keep provider definitions explicit and validated before relying on production failover paths.

### `models`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Model catalog root for provider definitions, merge/replace behavior, and optional Bedrock discovery integration. Keep provider definitions explicit and validated before relying on production failover paths.

### `models.bedrockDiscovery`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Automatic AWS Bedrock model discovery settings used to synthesize provider model entries from account visibility. Keep discovery scoped and refresh intervals conservative to reduce API churn.

### `models.bedrockDiscovery.defaultContextWindow`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Fallback context-window value applied to discovered models when provider metadata lacks explicit limits. Use realistic defaults to avoid oversized prompts that exceed true provider constraints.

### `models.bedrockDiscovery.defaultMaxTokens`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Fallback max-token value applied to discovered models without explicit output token limits. Use conservative defaults to reduce truncation surprises and unexpected token spend.

### `models.bedrockDiscovery.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Enables periodic Bedrock model discovery and catalog refresh for Bedrock-backed providers. Keep disabled unless Bedrock is actively used and IAM permissions are correctly configured.

### `models.bedrockDiscovery.providerFilter`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional provider allowlist filter for Bedrock discovery so only selected providers are refreshed. Use this to limit discovery scope in multi-provider environments.

### `models.bedrockDiscovery.providerFilter[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `models.bedrockDiscovery.refreshInterval`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Refresh cadence for Bedrock discovery polling in seconds to detect newly available models over time. Use longer intervals in production to reduce API cost and control-plane noise.

### `models.bedrockDiscovery.region`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: AWS region used for Bedrock discovery calls when discovery is enabled for your deployment. Use the region where your Bedrock models are provisioned to avoid empty discovery results.

### `models.mode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Controls provider catalog behavior: "merge" keeps built-ins and overlays your custom providers, while "replace" uses only your configured providers. Keep "merge" unless you intentionally want a strict custom list.

### `models.providers`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Provider map keyed by provider ID containing connection/auth settings and concrete model definitions. Use stable provider keys so references from agents and tooling remain portable across environments.

### `models.providers.*`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `models.providers.*.api`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Provider API adapter selection controlling request/response compatibility handling for model calls. Use the adapter that matches your upstream provider protocol to avoid feature mismatch.

### `models.providers.*.apiKey`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Provider credential used for API-key based authentication when the provider requires direct key auth. Use secret/env substitution and avoid storing real keys in committed config files.

### `models.providers.*.auth`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Selects provider auth style: "api-key" for API key auth, "token" for bearer token auth, "oauth" for OAuth credentials, and "aws-sdk" for AWS credential resolution. Match this to your provider requirements.

### `models.providers.*.authHeader`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: When true, credentials are sent via the HTTP Authorization header even if alternate auth is possible. Use this only when your provider or proxy explicitly requires Authorization forwarding.

### `models.providers.*.baseUrl`

- Type: `string`
- Required: yes
- Default: _none_
- Description: Base URL for the provider endpoint used to serve model requests for that provider entry. Use HTTPS endpoints and keep URLs environment-specific through config templating where needed.

### `models.providers.*.headers`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Static HTTP headers merged into provider requests for tenant routing, proxy auth, or custom gateway requirements. Use this sparingly and keep sensitive header values in secrets.

### `models.providers.*.headers.*`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `models.providers.*.models`

- Type: `array<object>`
- Required: yes
- Default: _none_
- Description: Declared model list for a provider including identifiers, metadata, and optional compatibility/cost hints. Keep IDs exact to provider catalog values so selection and fallback resolve correctly.

### `models.providers.*.models[]`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `models.providers.*.models[].api`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

## Node Host

Node host controls for features exposed from this gateway node to other nodes or clients. Keep defaults unless you intentionally proxy local capabilities across your node network.

### `nodeHost`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Node host controls for features exposed from this gateway node to other nodes or clients. Keep defaults unless you intentionally proxy local capabilities across your node network.

### `nodeHost.browserProxy`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Groups browser-proxy settings for exposing local browser control through node routing. Enable only when remote node workflows need your local browser profiles.

### `nodeHost.browserProxy.allowProfiles`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional allowlist of browser profile names exposed through node proxy routing. Leave empty to expose all configured profiles, or use a tight list to enforce least-privilege profile access.

### `nodeHost.browserProxy.allowProfiles[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `nodeHost.browserProxy.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Expose the local browser control server through node proxy routing so remote clients can use this host's browser capabilities. Keep disabled unless remote automation explicitly depends on it.

## Plugins

Plugin system controls for enabling extensions, constraining load scope, configuring entries, and tracking installs. Keep plugin policy explicit and least-privilege in production environments.

### `plugins`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Plugin system controls for enabling extensions, constraining load scope, configuring entries, and tracking installs. Keep plugin policy explicit and least-privilege in production environments.

### `plugins.allow`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional allowlist of plugin IDs; when set, only listed plugins are eligible to load. Use this to enforce approved extension inventories in controlled environments.

### `plugins.allow[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `plugins.deny`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional denylist of plugin IDs that are blocked even if allowlists or paths include them. Use deny rules for emergency rollback and hard blocks on risky plugins.

### `plugins.deny[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `plugins.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Enable or disable plugin/extension loading globally during startup and config reload (default: true). Keep enabled only when extension capabilities are required by your deployment.

### `plugins.entries`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Per-plugin settings keyed by plugin ID including enablement and plugin-specific runtime configuration payloads. Use this for scoped plugin tuning without changing global loader policy.

### `plugins.entries.*`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `plugins.entries.*.config`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Plugin-defined configuration payload interpreted by that plugin's own schema and validation rules. Use only documented fields from the plugin to prevent ignored or invalid settings.

### `plugins.entries.*.config.*`

- Type: `any`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `plugins.entries.*.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Per-plugin enablement override for a specific entry, applied on top of global plugin policy (restart required). Use this to stage plugin rollout gradually across environments.

### `plugins.installs`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: CLI-managed install metadata (used by `openclaw plugins update` to locate install sources).

### `plugins.installs.*`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `plugins.installs.*.installedAt`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: ISO timestamp of last install/update.

### `plugins.installs.*.installPath`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Resolved install directory (usually ~/.openclaw/extensions/\<id\>).

### `plugins.installs.*.integrity`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Resolved npm dist integrity hash for the fetched artifact (if reported by npm).

### `plugins.installs.*.resolvedAt`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: ISO timestamp when npm package metadata was last resolved for this install record.

### `plugins.installs.*.resolvedName`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Resolved npm package name from the fetched artifact.

### `plugins.installs.*.resolvedSpec`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Resolved exact npm spec (\<name\>@\<version\>) from the fetched artifact.

### `plugins.installs.*.resolvedVersion`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Resolved npm package version from the fetched artifact (useful for non-pinned specs).

### `plugins.installs.*.shasum`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Resolved npm dist shasum for the fetched artifact (if reported by npm).

### `plugins.installs.*.source`

- Type: `string`
- Required: yes
- Default: _none_
- Description: Install source ("npm", "archive", or "path").

### `plugins.installs.*.sourcePath`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Original archive/path used for install (if any).

### `plugins.installs.*.spec`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Original npm spec used for install (if source is npm).

### `plugins.installs.*.version`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Version recorded at install time (if available).

### `plugins.load`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Plugin loader configuration group for specifying filesystem paths where plugins are discovered. Keep load paths explicit and reviewed to avoid accidental untrusted extension loading.

### `plugins.load.paths`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Additional plugin files or directories scanned by the loader beyond built-in defaults. Use dedicated extension directories and avoid broad paths with unrelated executable content.

### `plugins.load.paths[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `plugins.slots`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Selects which plugins own exclusive runtime slots such as memory so only one plugin provides that capability. Use explicit slot ownership to avoid overlapping providers with conflicting behavior.

### `plugins.slots.memory`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Select the active memory plugin by id, or "none" to disable memory plugins.

## Session

Global session routing, reset, delivery policy, and maintenance controls for conversation history behavior. Keep defaults unless you need stricter isolation, retention, or delivery constraints.

### `session`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Global session routing, reset, delivery policy, and maintenance controls for conversation history behavior. Keep defaults unless you need stricter isolation, retention, or delivery constraints.

### `session.agentToAgent`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Groups controls for inter-agent session exchanges, including loop prevention limits on reply chaining. Keep defaults unless you run advanced agent-to-agent automation with strict turn caps.

### `session.agentToAgent.maxPingPongTurns`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Max reply-back turns between requester and target agents during agent-to-agent exchanges (0-5). Use lower values to hard-limit chatter loops and preserve predictable run completion.

### `session.dmScope`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: DM session scoping: "main" keeps continuity, while "per-peer", "per-channel-peer", and "per-account-channel-peer" increase isolation. Use isolated modes for shared inboxes or multi-account deployments.

### `session.identityLinks`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Maps canonical identities to provider-prefixed peer IDs so equivalent users resolve to one DM thread (example: telegram:123456). Use this when the same human appears across multiple channels or accounts.

### `session.identityLinks.*`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `session.identityLinks.*[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `session.idleMinutes`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Applies a legacy idle reset window in minutes for session reuse behavior across inactivity gaps. Use this only for compatibility and prefer structured reset policies under session.reset/session.resetByType.

### `session.mainKey`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Overrides the canonical main session key used for continuity when dmScope or routing logic points to "main". Use a stable value only if you intentionally need custom session anchoring.

### `session.maintenance`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Automatic session-store maintenance controls for pruning age, entry caps, and file rotation behavior. Start in warn mode to observe impact, then enforce once thresholds are tuned.

### `session.maintenance.maxEntries`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Caps total session entry count retained in the store to prevent unbounded growth over time. Use lower limits for constrained environments, or higher limits when longer history is required.

### `session.maintenance.mode`

- Type: `"enforce" | "warn"`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Determines whether maintenance policies are only reported ("warn") or actively applied ("enforce"). Keep "warn" during rollout and switch to "enforce" after validating safe thresholds.

### `session.maintenance.pruneAfter`

- Type: `string | number`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Removes entries older than this duration (for example `30d` or `12h`) during maintenance passes. Use this as the primary age-retention control and align it with data retention policy.

### `session.maintenance.pruneDays`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Deprecated age-retention field kept for compatibility with legacy configs using day counts. Use session.maintenance.pruneAfter instead so duration syntax and behavior are consistent.

### `session.maintenance.rotateBytes`

- Type: `string | number`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Rotates the session store when file size exceeds a threshold such as `10mb` or `1gb`. Use this to bound single-file growth and keep backup/restore operations manageable.

### `session.reset`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Defines the default reset policy object used when no type-specific or channel-specific override applies. Set this first, then layer resetByType or resetByChannel only where behavior must differ.

### `session.resetByChannel`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Provides channel-specific reset overrides keyed by provider/channel id for fine-grained behavior control. Use this only when one channel needs exceptional reset behavior beyond type-level policies.

### `session.resetByChannel.*`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `session.resetByChannel.*.atHour`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `session.resetByChannel.*.idleMinutes`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `session.resetByChannel.*.mode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `session.resetByType`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Overrides reset behavior by chat type (direct, group, thread) when defaults are not sufficient. Use this when group/thread traffic needs different reset cadence than direct messages.

### `session.resetByType.direct`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Defines reset policy for direct chats and supersedes the base session.reset configuration for that type. Use this as the canonical direct-message override instead of the legacy dm alias.

### `session.resetByType.dm`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Deprecated alias for direct reset behavior kept for backward compatibility with older configs. Use session.resetByType.direct instead so future tooling and validation remain consistent.

### `session.resetByType.group`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Defines reset policy for group chat sessions where continuity and noise patterns differ from DMs. Use shorter idle windows for busy groups if context drift becomes a problem.

### `session.resetByType.thread`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Defines reset policy for thread-scoped sessions, including focused channel thread workflows. Use this when thread sessions should expire faster or slower than other chat types.

### `session.resetTriggers`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Lists message triggers that force a session reset when matched in inbound content. Use sparingly for explicit reset phrases so context is not dropped unexpectedly during normal conversation.

### `session.resetTriggers[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `session.scope`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sets base session grouping strategy: "per-sender" isolates by sender and "global" shares one session per channel context. Keep "per-sender" for safer multi-user behavior unless deliberate shared context is required.

### `session.sendPolicy`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Controls cross-session send permissions using allow/deny rules evaluated against channel, chatType, and key prefixes. Use this to fence where session tools can deliver messages in complex environments.

### `session.store`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sets the session storage file path used to persist session records across restarts. Use an explicit path only when you need custom disk layout, backup routing, or mounted-volume storage.

### `session.threadBindings`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Shared defaults for thread-bound session routing behavior across providers that support thread focus workflows. Configure global defaults here and override per channel only when behavior differs.

### `session.threadBindings.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Global master switch for thread-bound session routing features and focused thread delivery behavior. Keep enabled for modern thread workflows unless you need to disable thread binding globally.

### `session.threadBindings.ttlHours`

- Type: `number`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Default auto-unfocus TTL in hours for thread-bound sessions across providers/channels (0 disables). Keep 24h-like values for practical focus windows unless your team needs longer-lived thread binding.

### `session.typingIntervalSeconds`

- Type: `integer`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Controls interval for repeated typing indicators while replies are being prepared in typing-capable channels. Increase to reduce chatty updates or decrease for more active typing feedback.

### `session.typingMode`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Controls typing behavior timing: "never", "instant", "thinking", or "message" based emission points. Keep conservative modes in high-volume channels to avoid unnecessary typing noise.

## Talk

Talk-mode voice synthesis settings for voice identity, model selection, output format, and interruption behavior. Use this section to tune human-facing voice UX while controlling latency and cost.

### `talk`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Talk-mode voice synthesis settings for voice identity, model selection, output format, and interruption behavior. Use this section to tune human-facing voice UX while controlling latency and cost.

### `talk.apiKey`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional talk-provider API key override used specifically for speech synthesis requests. Use env-backed secrets and set this only when talk traffic must use separate credentials.

### `talk.interruptOnSpeech`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: When true, interrupts current speech playback on new speech/input events for more conversational turn-taking. Keep enabled for interactive voice UX and disable for uninterrupted long-form playback.

### `talk.modelId`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Model override used for talk pipeline generation when voice workflows require different model behavior. Use this when speech output needs a specialized low-latency or style-tuned model.

### `talk.outputFormat`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Audio output format for synthesized talk responses, depending on provider support and client playback expectations. Use formats compatible with your playback channel to avoid decode failures.

### `talk.voiceAliases`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Alias map for human-friendly voice shortcuts to concrete voice IDs in talk workflows. Use aliases to simplify operator switching without exposing long provider-native IDs.

### `talk.voiceAliases.*`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `talk.voiceId`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Primary voice identifier used by talk mode when synthesizing spoken responses. Use a stable voice for consistent persona and switch only when experience goals change.

## Tools

Global tool access policy and capability configuration across web, exec, media, messaging, and elevated surfaces. Use this section to constrain risky capabilities before broad rollout.

### `tools`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Global tool access policy and capability configuration across web, exec, media, messaging, and elevated surfaces. Use this section to constrain risky capabilities before broad rollout.

### `tools.agentToAgent`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Policy for allowing agent-to-agent tool calls and constraining which target agents can be reached. Keep disabled or tightly scoped unless cross-agent orchestration is intentionally enabled.

### `tools.agentToAgent.allow`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Allowlist of target agent IDs permitted for agent_to_agent calls when orchestration is enabled. Use explicit allowlists to avoid uncontrolled cross-agent call graphs.

### `tools.agentToAgent.allow[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `tools.agentToAgent.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Enables the agent_to_agent tool surface so one agent can invoke another agent at runtime. Keep off in simple deployments and enable only when orchestration value outweighs complexity.

### `tools.allow`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Absolute tool allowlist that replaces profile-derived defaults for strict environments. Use this only when you intentionally run a tightly curated subset of tool capabilities.

### `tools.allow[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `tools.alsoAllow`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Extra tool allowlist entries merged on top of the selected tool profile and default policy. Keep this list small and explicit so audits can quickly identify intentional policy exceptions.

### `tools.alsoAllow[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `tools.byProvider`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Per-provider tool allow/deny overrides keyed by channel/provider ID to tailor capabilities by surface. Use this when one provider needs stricter controls than global tool policy.

### `tools.byProvider.*`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `tools.byProvider.*.alsoAllow`

- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

- Default: _none_

- Default: _none_

### `tools.deny`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Global tool denylist that blocks listed tools even when profile or provider rules would allow them. Use deny rules for emergency lockouts and long-term defense-in-depth.

### `tools.deny[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `tools.elevated`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Elevated tool access controls for privileged command surfaces that should only be reachable from trusted senders. Keep disabled unless operator workflows explicitly require elevated actions.

### `tools.elevated.allowFrom`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Sender allow rules for elevated tools, usually keyed by channel/provider identity formats. Use narrow, explicit identities so elevated commands cannot be triggered by unintended users.

- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `tools.elevated.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Enables elevated tool execution path when sender and policy checks pass. Keep disabled in public/shared channels and enable only for trusted owner-operated contexts.

### `tools.exec`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Exec-tool policy grouping for shell execution host, security mode, approval behavior, and runtime bindings. Keep conservative defaults in production and tighten elevated execution paths.

### `tools.exec.applyPatch`

- Type: `object`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `tools.exec.applyPatch.allowModels`

- Type: `array<string>`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Optional allowlist of model ids (e.g. "gpt-5.2" or "openai/gpt-5.2").

### `tools.exec.applyPatch.allowModels[]`

- Type: `string`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: _No description provided._

### `tools.exec.applyPatch.enabled`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Experimental. Enables apply_patch for OpenAI models when allowed by tool policy.

### `tools.exec.applyPatch.workspaceOnly`

- Type: `boolean`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Restrict apply_patch paths to the workspace directory (default: true). Set false to allow writing outside the workspace (dangerous).

### `tools.exec.ask`

- Type: `"off" | "on-miss" | "always"`
- Required: no
- Default: _none_
- Description: Approval strategy for when exec commands require human confirmation before running. Use stricter ask behavior in shared channels and lower-friction settings in private operator contexts.

### `tools.exec.backgroundMs`

- Default: _none_

### `tools.exec.host`
